## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Solid Mechanics, specifically, Material Modeling
**Analysis**: The task involves modeling the stress-strain relationship of a material at different temperatures, which is a common problem in material science and engineering. The goal is to identify a mathematical relationship between the stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T) of the material.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Lamé's equation: sigma = c1 * (1 + epsilon)^c2 * exp(c3 * T) (relationship between stress, strain, and temperature for isotropic elastic materials)
- Hook's law: epsilon = c1 * sigma / E (linear relationship between strain and stress for elastic materials, temperature-independent)
- Ramberg-Osgood model: epsilon = c1 * sigma + c2 * sigma**c3 (nonlinear relationship between strain and stress for plastic materials)
- JWL equation: sigma = c1 * (1 + c2 * epsilon)**c3 * exp(c4 * T) (high-strain rate model for explosive materials)
- Eyring model: sigma = c1 * exp(c2 * T) * (1 - exp(c3 * epsilon)) (temperature-dependent model for plastic deformation)
- Gibbs free energy: delta G = c1 * T * delta S - c2 * delta V + c3 * delta epsilon (Gibbs free energy change for material deformation)
- Cauchy stress tensor: sigma = c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 (isotropic elastic model for 2D materials)
- Gurson-Tvergaard-Needleman model: sigma = c1 * epsilon + c2 * (epsilon**2 - c3**2) / (1 - c4 * epsilon) (ductile fracture model for porous materials)
- Kelvin-Voigt model: sigma = c1 * epsilon + c2 * d**(-1) (viscoelastic model for rate-dependent materials)
- von Mises stress: sigma = sqrt((c1 * epsilon_1 - c2 * epsilon_2)**2 + (c3 * epsilon_1 + c4 * epsilon_2)**2) (damage model for composite materials)
- Tsai-Hill criterion: sigma = c1 * epsilon_1 + c2 * epsilon_2 + c3 * epsilon_3 + c4 * epsilon_1 * epsilon_2 + c5 * epsilon_1 * epsilon_3 + c6 * epsilon_2 * epsilon_3 (failure criterion for fiber-reinforced composites)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Viscoelastic behavior → Kelvin-Voigt or Maxwell model, involving exponential decay or sum of exponential terms
- Plastic deformation → Ramberg-Osgood model, power-law or exponential relationship between strain and stress
- Damage or failure → von Mises or Tsai-Hill criterion, involving combinations of terms with different powers of strain
- Anisotropic materials → Cauchy stress tensor or Gibbs free energy, involving different coefficients for different strain components
- High-strain rate or shock loading → JWL or other high-strain rate models, involving rapid changes in stress and strain
- Non-isothermal conditions → Eyring or other temperature-dependent models, involving exponential relationships between stress and temperature
- Material instabilities → Gurson-Tvergaard-Needleman or other ductile fracture models, involving terms with different powers of strain
- Empirical fitting → Hook's law or other simple, linear relationships, when exact physical behavior is unknown or uncertain

After systematically analyzing all 51 candidates against the Ground Truth (GT) expression, we find that none can be made exactly equivalent under the given rules.

**Ground Truth Structure:**  
GT = `c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + c4*epsilon**3 + c6*(T - c2)*sin(epsilon)`  
With `c2 = c7`, this simplifies to terms linear in `T` (`T*epsilon`, `T*sin(epsilon)`) plus terms independent of `T` (`epsilon`, `epsilon**3`, `sin(epsilon)`). No other functions (exponentials, logs, rational denominators) appear, and `sin(epsilon)` appears both with and without a `T` multiplier.

**Common reasons for rejection:**
- Many candidates lack `sin` entirely or contain only `sin` without `T*sin` (e.g., Candidates 1–3, 23).
- Candidates with `sin`/`cos` and `T` either lack the pure `epsilon**3` polynomial term (Candidate 4) or have an irreducible global `epsilon` factor that forces all terms to include `epsilon`, making it impossible to match the standalone `sin(epsilon)` and `T*sin(epsilon)` terms (Candidates 39, 41).
- Numerous candidates introduce functions absent from the GT (exponentials, logs, hyperbolic tangents, rational denominators in `T`) that cannot be eliminated without zeroing out necessary terms.
- Candidates without any `T` dependence (e.g., 11, 12, 19–21, 23, 25, 26, 30, 32, 33, 35, 36, 38, 46, 48) cannot match the GT’s explicit `T`-dependent terms.

No candidate successfully reproduces the exact polynomial plus sinusoidal structure of the GT.
